           </dd>
          </dl> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Additional emoji can be found in the following Unicode blocks: <a href="/wiki/Arrows_(Unicode_block)" title="Arrows (Unicode block)">Arrows</a> (8 code points considered emoji), <a href="/wiki/Basic_Latin_(Unicode_block)" title="Basic Latin (Unicode block)">Basic Latin</a> (12), <a href="/wiki/CJK_Symbols_and_Punctuation" title="CJK Symbols and Punctuation">CJK Symbols and Punctuation</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Enclosed_Alphanumeric_Supplement" title="Enclosed Alphanumeric Supplement">Enclosed Alphanumeric Supplement</a> (41), <a href="/wiki/Enclosed_Alphanumerics" title="Enclosed Alphanumerics">Enclosed Alphanumerics</a> (1), <a href="/wiki/Enclosed_CJK_Letters_and_Months" title="Enclosed CJK Letters and Months">Enclosed CJK Letters and Months</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Enclosed_Ideographic_Supplement" title="Enclosed Ideographic Supplement">Enclosed Ideographic Supplement</a> (15), <a href="/wiki/General_Punctuation" title="General Punctuation">General Punctuation</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Geometric_Shapes" title="Geometric Shapes">Geometric Shapes</a> (8), <a href="/wiki/Geometric_Shapes_Extended" title="Geometric Shapes Extended">Geometric Shapes Extended</a> (12), <a href="/wiki/Latin-1_Supplement_(Unicode_block)" title="Latin-1 Supplement (Unicode block)">Latin-1 Supplement</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Letterlike_Symbols" title="Letterlike Symbols">Letterlike Symbols</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Mahjong_Tiles_(Unicode_block)" title="Mahjong Tiles (Unicode block)">Mahjong Tiles</a> (1), <a href="/wiki/Miscellaneous_Symbols_and_Arrows_(Unicode_block)" class="mw-redirect" title="Miscellaneous Symbols and Arrows (Unicode block)">Miscellaneous Symbols and Arrows</a> (7), <a href="/wiki/Miscellaneous_Technical" title="Miscellaneous Technical">Miscellaneous Technical</a> (18), <a href="/wiki/Playing_cards_in_Unicode" title="Playing cards in Unicode">Playing Cards</a> (1), and <a href="/wiki/Supplemental_Arrows-B_(Unicode_block)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supplemental Arrows-B (Unicode block)">Supplemental Arrows-B</a> (2). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Additions">Additions</span></h3> 
      <p>Some vendors, most notably Microsoft, Samsung and <a href="/wiki/HTC" title="HTC">HTC</a>, add emoji presentation to some other existing Unicode characters or coin their own ZWJ sequences. </p>
      <p>Microsoft displays all <a href="/wiki/Mahjong_Tiles_(Unicode_block)" title="Mahjong Tiles (Unicode block)">Mahjong tiles</a> (U+1F000?2B, not just <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+1F004</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">MAHJONG TILE RED DRAGON</span>) and alternative card suits (<span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2661</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2662</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2664</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2666</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>) as emoji. They also support additional pencils (<span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+270E</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2710</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>) and a heart-shaped bullet (<span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2765</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>). </p>
      <p>While only <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+261D</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span> is officially an emoji, Microsoft and Samsung add the other three directions as well (<span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+261C</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+261E</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+261F</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>). Both vendors pair the standard checked ballot box emoji <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2611</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span> with its crossed variant <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2612</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>, but only Samsung also has the empty ballot box <span class="nowrap">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734"><span class="monospaced">U+2610</span> </span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">?</span> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span>. </p>
      <p>Samsung almost completely covers the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Miscellaneous_Symbols" title="Miscellaneous Symbols">Miscellaneous Symbols</a> block (U+2600?FF) as emoji, which includes Chess pieces, game die faces, some traffic sign as well as genealogical and astronomical symbols for instance. </p>
      <p>HTC supports most additional pictographs from the <a href="/wiki/Miscellaneous_Symbols_and_Pictographs" title="Miscellaneous Symbols and Pictographs">Miscellaneous Symbols and Pictographs</a> (U+1F300?5FF) and <a href="/wiki/Transport_and_Map_Symbols" title="Transport and Map Symbols">Transport and Map Symbols</a> (U+1F680?FF) blocks. Some of them are also shown as emoji on Samsung devices. </p>
      <p>The open source projects Emojidex and Emojitwo are trying to cover all of these extensions established by major vendors. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementation">Implementation</span></h2> 
      <p>The exact appearance of emoji is not prescribed but varies between fonts, in the same way that normal typefaces can display letters differently. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Color_Emoji" title="Apple Color Emoji">Apple Color Emoji</a> typeface is proprietary to Apple, and can only be used on Apple devices (without additional <a href="/wiki/Hacker_culture#Programming" title="Hacker culture">hacking</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Different computing companies have developed their own fonts to display emoji, some of which have been <a href="/wiki/Open_source_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source software">open-sourced</a> to permit their reuse.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Both colour and monochrome emoji typefaces exist, as well as at least one animated design.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_aspects">Technical aspects</span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Supplementary_Multilingual_Plane_support">Supplementary Multilingual Plane support</span></h4> 
      <p>Most, but not all, emoji are included in the <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_Multilingual_Plane" class="mw-redirect" title="Supplementary Multilingual Plane">Supplementary Multilingual Plane</a> (SMP) of Unicode. The SMP also includes, for example, ancient scripts such as <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform_(Unicode_block)" title="Cuneiform (Unicode block)">Cuneiform</a> or <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Hieroglyphs_(Unicode_block)" title="Egyptian Hieroglyphs (Unicode block)">Egyptian hieroglyphs</a>, some modern scripts such as <a href="/wiki/Adlam_(Unicode_block)" title="Adlam (Unicode block)">Adlam</a> or <a href="/wiki/Osage_(Unicode_block)" title="Osage (Unicode block)">Osage</a>, and special-use characters such as <a href="/wiki/Musical_Symbols_(Unicode_block)" title="Musical Symbols (Unicode block)">Musical Symbols</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_Alphanumeric_Symbols" title="Mathematical Alphanumeric Symbols">Mathematical Alphanumeric Symbols</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unicode was originally designed as a 16-bit encoding, which could be represented in a pure 16-bit form known as <a href="/wiki/UCS-2" class="mw-redirect" title="UCS-2">UCS-2</a>. This corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/Basic_Multilingual_Plane" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic Multilingual Plane">Basic Multilingual Plane</a> (BMP) of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Coded_Character_Set" title="Universal Coded Character Set">Universal Coded Character Set</a>. In Unicode 2.0, this was expanded to 17 planes (numbered 0 through 16, where the BMP is plane 0), and the first non-BMP characters were allocated in Unicode 3.1.<sup id="cite_ref-lundeastral_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lundeastral-124">[123]</a></sup> UCS-2 is now obsolete and <a href="/wiki/Deprecated" class="mw-redirect" title="Deprecated">deprecated</a> in favour of <a href="/wiki/UTF-16" title="UTF-16">UTF-16</a>, a variable-width encoding which follows UCS-2 for the BMP, but extends it with four-byte codes representing non-BMP characters. Non-BMP characters (in the SMP and in other supplementary planes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_Ideographic_Plane" class="mw-redirect" title="Supplementary Ideographic Plane">Supplementary Ideographic Plane</a>) now number in the tens of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-lundeastral_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lundeastral-124">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some systems introduced prior to the advent of Unicode emoji were only designed to support characters in the BMP, on the assumption that non-BMP characters would rarely be encountered,<sup id="cite_ref-backendless_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backendless-61">[60]</a></sup> although failure to properly handle characters outside of the BMP precludes Unicode compliance.<sup id="cite_ref-lundeastral_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lundeastral-124">[123]</a></sup> For example, earlier versions of <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> supported <a href="/wiki/UCS-2" class="mw-redirect" title="UCS-2">UCS-2</a> and a variant of <a href="/wiki/UTF-8" title="UTF-8">UTF-8</a> excluding four-byte codes, thus not handling non-BMP characters correctly. Support for <a href="/wiki/UTF-32" title="UTF-32">UTF-32</a> and full support for <a href="/wiki/UTF-16" title="UTF-16">UTF-16</a> and UTF-8 (under the name <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">utf8mb4</code>) was added in version 5.5,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> with <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">utf8</code> retained as an alias for the up-to-three-byte version, although this is intended to be changed in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The introduction of Unicode emoji created an incentive for vendors to improve their support for non-BMP characters.<sup id="cite_ref-backendless_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backendless-61">[60]</a></sup> The Unicode Consortium notes that "[b]ecause of the demand for emoji, many implementations have upgraded their Unicode support substantially."<sup id="cite_ref-detract_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detract-60">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Font_format_support">Font format support</span></h4> 
      <p>Any operating system that supports adding additional fonts to the system can add an emoji-supporting font. However, inclusion of colorful emoji in existing font formats requires dedicated support for color <a href="/wiki/Glyphs" class="mw-redirect" title="Glyphs">glyphs</a>. Not all operating systems have support for color fonts, so in these cases emoji might have to be rendered as black-and-white line art or not at all. There are four different formats used for multi-color glyphs in an <a href="/wiki/SFNT" title="SFNT">SFNT</a> font.<sup id="cite_ref-mscolotf_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mscolotf-127">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/OpenType" title="OpenType">OpenType</a> version 1.8 standardizes all four. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CBDT</code><sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> is a multi-color <a href="/wiki/Raster_graphics" title="Raster graphics">raster</a> format, using raw bitmap data or embedded <a href="/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" title="Portable Network Graphics">PNG</a> data.<sup id="cite_ref-cbdt_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbdt-129">[128]</a></sup> It requires an auxiliary <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CBLC</code> table to hold details about the image format,<sup id="cite_ref-cbdt_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbdt-129">[128]</a></sup> and as such the format is sometimes called "CBDT/CBLC".<sup id="cite_ref-mscolotf_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mscolotf-127">[126]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">COLR</code><sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> is a multi-color <a href="/wiki/Vector_graphics" title="Vector graphics">vector</a> format, using multiple single-color <a href="/wiki/OpenType" title="OpenType">OpenType</a> (<a href="/wiki/TrueType" title="TrueType">TrueType</a> or <a href="/wiki/Compact_Font_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Compact Font Format">CFF</a>) glyphs. A number of glyphs are assigned individual block colours and layered, and associated with a specified single-colour base glyph. The layered glyphs are shown instead of the base glyph when the character is displayed as multi-color.<sup id="cite_ref-colr_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colr-130">[129]</a></sup> Colors are referenced from a palette, which is defined in a separate <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CPAL</code> table,<sup id="cite_ref-colr_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colr-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cpal_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpal-131">[130]</a></sup> and as such the format is sometimes called "COLR/CPAL".<sup id="cite_ref-mscolotf_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mscolotf-127">[126]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">sbix</code> is a multi-color raster format, using embedded <a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a>, PNG or <a href="/wiki/TIFF" title="TIFF">TIFF</a> images. Including multi-color raster or vector glyphs as embedded <a href="/wiki/PDF" title="PDF">PDF</a> files is also permitted by the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Advanced_Typography" title="Apple Advanced Typography">Apple Advanced Typography</a> specification, but not by the OpenType specification, and is planned for future releases of <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>SVG-in-OpenType (or OpenType-SVG) is a multi-color vector format (with support for embedded rasters),<sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> using embedded <a href="/wiki/SVG" class="mw-redirect" title="SVG">SVG</a> images. It requires the inclusion of a single-color TrueType or CFF glyph as well, serving as a fallback.<sup id="cite_ref-svginotf_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-svginotf-134">[133]</a></sup> Being based on SVG, it includes support for <a href="/wiki/Color_gradient" title="Color gradient">color gradients</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-svginotf_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-svginotf-134">[133]</a></sup> An OpenType-SVG font may use a <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CPAL</code> palette, similarly to <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">COLR</code>; however, this is not required.<sup id="cite_ref-cpal_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpal-131">[130]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">COLR</code> format was introduced by Microsoft, with <a href="/wiki/Windows_8.1" title="Windows 8.1">Windows 8.1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mscolotf_127-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mscolotf-127">[126]</a></sup> The <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CBDT</code> format was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and is supported on <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, while the competing <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">sbix</code> format was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, and is supported on <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>. SVG-in-OpenType was designed by <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Inc." title="Adobe Inc.">Adobe</a> as an industry standard.<sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some support for SVG-in-OpenType support has been added to newer updates of <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a>, and to newer versions of iOS and macOS.<sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/DirectWrite" title="DirectWrite">DirectWrite</a> has supported all four since Windows 10 Anniversary Update; however, Windows only supports a subset of SVG-in-OpenType.<sup id="cite_ref-mscolotf_127-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mscolotf-127">[126]</a></sup> On the web, SVG-in-OpenType is supported by recent versions of <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Safari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a>, but not by <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a>; Edge and Safari additionally support <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">sbix</code>, while Edge and Chrome support <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CBDT</code> and all four support <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr">COLR</code>.<sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This means that color fonts may need to be supplied in several formats to be usable on multiple operating systems, or in multiple applications. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internationalized_domain_names">Internationalized domain names</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Emoji_domain" title="Emoji domain">Emoji domain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internationalized_domain_name" title="Internationalized domain name">Internationalized domain name</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A limited number of <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domains</a> allow registration of domain names containing emoji characters. Emoji-containing subdomains are also possible under any top-level domain. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vendors_and_platforms">Vendors and platforms</span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Google_.28Android_and_Chrome_OS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Google_(Android_and_Chrome_OS)">Google (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1023754711">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="Android"></span><span class="vanchor-text">Android</span></span> and 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1023754711"><span class="vanchor"><span id="Chrome_OS"></span><span class="vanchor-text">Chrome OS</span></span>)</span></h4> 
      <p>Google's <a href="/wiki/Noto_fonts" title="Noto fonts">Noto fonts</a> project includes the Noto Color Emoji font, which supplies colour glyphs for emoji characters.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chrome_OS" title="Chrome OS">Chrome OS</a>, through its inclusion of the Noto fonts, supports the emoji set introduced through Unicode 6.2. As of Chrome OS 41, Noto Color Emoji is the default font for most emoji. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> devices support emoji differently depending on the operating system version. Google added native emoji support to Android in July 2013 with Android 4.3,<sup id="cite_ref-CNet_4.3_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNet_4.3-136">[135]</a></sup> and to the Google Keyboard in November 2013 for devices running Android 4.4 and later.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> Android 7.0 Nougat added Unicode 9 emoji, skin tone modifiers, and a redesign of many existing emoji.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Emoji are also supported by the <a href="/wiki/Google_Hangouts" title="Google Hangouts">Google Hangouts</a> application (independent of the keyboard in use), in both Hangouts and <a href="/wiki/Text_messaging" title="Text messaging">SMS</a> modes.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Several third-party messaging and keyboard applications (such as IQQI Keyboard) for Android devices<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> provide plugins that allow the use of emoji. Some apps, e.g. <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">WhatsApp</a>, come with Apple emoji for internal use.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> With Android 8 (Oreo), Google added a compatibility library that, if included by app developers, makes the latest Noto emoji available on any platform since Android 4.3.<sup id="cite_ref-EmojiCompat_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmojiCompat-141">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Stock Android systems include the Noto glyphs for emoji characters, although individual social media apps may use their own glyphs instead.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> However, mobile phone vendors HTC and LG deployed variants of NotoColorEmoji.ttf with custom glyphs prior to 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> and Samsung still does.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> Some Japanese mobile carriers used to equip branded Android devices with emoji glyphs that were closer to the original ones, but apparently have stopped updating these circa 2015.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Apple">Apple</span></h4> 
      <p>Apple first introduced emoji to their desktop operating system with the release of <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">OS X</a> <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Lion" title="Mac OS X Lion">10.7 Lion</a>, in 2011. Users can view emoji characters sent through email and messaging applications, which are commonly shared by mobile users, as well as any other application. Users can create emoji symbols using the "Characters" special input panel from almost any native application by selecting the "Edit" menu and pulling down to "Special Characters", or by the key combination <kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">? Command</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">? Option</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">T</kbd>. Users can also create these symbols by switching the keyboard to Unicode, holding <kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">? Option</kbd> and typing the Unicode hex input. For example, holding down <kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">? Option</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">2</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">6</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">3</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">A</kbd> would create ?. The desktop OS uses the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Color_Emoji" title="Apple Color Emoji">Apple Color Emoji</a> font that was introduced earlier in <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>. This provides users with full color pictographs.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The emoji keyboard was first available in Japan with the release of <a href="/wiki/IPhone_OS_2" title="IPhone OS 2">iPhone OS version 2.2</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> The emoji keyboard was not officially made available outside of Japan until <a href="/wiki/IOS_5" title="IOS 5">iOS version 5.0</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> From iPhone OS 2.2 through to iOS 4.3.5 (2011), those outside Japan could access the keyboard but had to use a third party app to enable it. The first of such apps was developed by <a href="/wiki/Josh_Gare" title="Josh Gare">Josh Gare</a>; emoji beginning to be embraced by popular culture outside Japan has been attributed to these apps.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> iOS was updated to support <a href="/wiki/Fitzpatrick_scale" title="Fitzpatrick scale">Fitzpatrick skin-tone modifiers</a> with version 8.3.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/OS_X_Mavericks" title="OS X Mavericks">OS X 10.9 Mavericks</a> introduced a dedicated emoji input palette in most text input boxes using the key combination <kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">? Command</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">Ctrl</kbd>+<kbd class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.1em 0.2em rgba(0,0,0,0.1); background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); color: #000; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.85em;">Space</kbd>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Apple has revealed that the "face with tears of joy" is the most popular emoji among English speaking Americans. On second place is the "heart" emoji followed by the "Loudly Crying Face".<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On July 17, 2018, for the <a href="/wiki/World_Emoji_Day" title="World Emoji Day">World Emoji Day</a>, Apple announced that it will be adding 70 more emoji in its 2018 <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> update, including the long-awaited, red hair, white hair, curly hair and bald emoji.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On September 12, 2017, Apple announced that the <a href="/wiki/Messages_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Messages (software)">Messages</a> app on the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhones</a> with <a href="/wiki/Face_ID" title="Face ID">Face ID</a> would get "Animoji", which are versions of standard emoji that are custom-animated with the use of <a href="/wiki/Facial_motion_capture" title="Facial motion capture">facial motion capture</a> to reflect the sender's expressions. These Animoji can also utilize <a href="/wiki/Lip_sync" title="Lip sync">lip sync</a> to appear to speak audio messages recorded by the sender. Apple had created 3D models of all standard emoji prior to its late-2016 OS updates from which the static default 2D graphics had been rendered. A select set of these models are being reused for creating still images and short animations dynamically. </p>
      <p>With the release of <a href="/wiki/IOS_13" title="IOS 13">iOS 13</a>, Apple introduced "Memoji" that allows the use of an avatar that a user can use to personalize messages; this feature does not require Face ID.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Linux">Linux</span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_version_history#Ubuntu_18.04_LTS_(Bionic_Beaver)" title="Ubuntu version history">Ubuntu 18.04</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fedora_(operating_system)" title="Fedora (operating system)">Fedora</a> 28 support color emoji by default, using <a href="/wiki/Noto_fonts" title="Noto fonts">Noto Color Emoji</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">Linux distributions</a> require the installation of extra fonts.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> Color emoji are supported by <a href="/wiki/FreeType" title="FreeType">FreeType</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cairo_(graphics)" title="Cairo (graphics)">Cairo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Microsoft_Windows">Microsoft Windows</span></h4> 
      <p>An update for <a href="/wiki/Windows_7" title="Windows 7">Windows 7</a> and Windows Server 2008 R2 brought a subset of the monochrome Unicode set to those operating systems as part of the <i>Segoe UI Symbol</i> font.<sup id="cite_ref-An_update_for_the_Segoe_UI_symbol_font_in_Windows_7_and_in_Windows_Server_2008_R2_is_available_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-An_update_for_the_Segoe_UI_symbol_font_in_Windows_7_and_in_Windows_Server_2008_R2_is_available-162">[161]</a></sup> As of <a href="/wiki/Windows_8.1" title="Windows 8.1">Windows 8.1</a> Preview, the <i>Segoe UI Emoji</i> font is included, which supplies full-color pictographs. The plain Segoe UI font lacks emoji characters, whereas Segoe UI Symbol and Segoe UI Emoji include them. </p>
      <p>Emoji characters are accessed through the onscreen keyboard's "smiley" key. </p>
      <p>Differently from macOS and iOS, color glyphs are only supplied when the application supports Microsoft's <a href="/wiki/DirectWrite" title="DirectWrite">DirectWrite</a> API, and Segoe UI Emoji is explicitly declared, otherwise monochrome glyphs appear.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> Microsoft's COLR/CPAL format for multi-color fonts such as Segoe UI Emoji is supported by the current versions of several web browsers on Windows (including <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_Explorer" title="Internet Explorer">Internet Explorer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a>), but not by many graphics applications.<sup id="cite_ref-cfwt_128-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfwt-128">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10 Anniversary Update</a> added Unicode 9 emoji.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_media_platforms">Social media platforms</span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> replace all Unicode emoji used on their websites with their own custom graphics. </p>
      <p>Prior to October 2017, Facebook had different sets for the main site and for its <a href="/wiki/Facebook_Messenger" title="Facebook Messenger">Messenger</a> service, where only the former provides complete coverage. Messenger now uses Apple emoji on iOS, and the main Facebook set elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Facebook_reactions" class="mw-redirect" title="Facebook reactions">Facebook reactions</a> are only partially compatible with standard emoji.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Twitter has released Twemoji, which is their emoji graphics together with a JavaScript library to handle them, under the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons_license" title="Creative Commons license">Creative Commons CC-BY 4.0 license</a> and the <a href="/wiki/MIT_License" title="MIT License">MIT open-source license</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> Despite this, the Android and iOS Twitter apps use the emoji graphics that are native to the platform they are running on (Apple and Google), instead of the Twemoji graphics. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_emoji_font_vendors"><span class="anchor" id="EmojiOne"></span><span class="anchor" id="EmojiTwo"></span><span class="anchor" id="JoyPixels"></span><span class="anchor" id="FxEmojis"></span><span class="anchor" id="FxEmoji"></span><span class="anchor" id="Mozilla"></span><span class="anchor" id="Symbola"></span><span class="anchor" id="Quivira"></span>Other emoji font vendors</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Emojione_1F3AB.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Emojione_1F3AB.svg/220px-Emojione_1F3AB.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Emojione_1F3AB.svg/330px-Emojione_1F3AB.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Emojione_1F3AB.svg/440px-Emojione_1F3AB.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Emojione_1F3AB.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>EmojiOne 2.2 logo on the <a href="/wiki/Ticket_(admission)" title="Ticket (admission)">ticket</a> emoji
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>EmojiOne version 2.2, an open-source font available under a <a href="/wiki/Free_content" title="Free content">free content</a> license, supports the full emoji set in color through Unicode Emoji 3.0, i.e. Unicode 9.0. Newer versions of EmojiOne, since renamed JoyPixels,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> support more recent Unicode Emoji versions, and use a stricter license that disallows the redistribution of vector images, while version 2.x is "no longer supported or distributed".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> EmojiTwo, an open-source fork of EmojiOne 2.2, aims to add all emoji from 2017 and later. </p>
      <p>As part of the now-discontinued <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">Firefox OS</a> project, <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a> developed an emoji font named FxEmojis.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> Mozilla also package a version of Twitter's Twemoji font converted to a COLR/CPAL layered format font, named "Twemoji Mozilla".<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> Older versions of the latter Mozilla project instead packaged the EmojiOne font, as "EmojiOne Mozilla".<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The font <i>Symbola</i> contains all emoji through version 10.0 as normal monochrome glyphs. Through version 10, Symbola was a <a href="/wiki/Open-source_Unicode_typefaces" title="Open-source Unicode typefaces">public domain font</a>; beginning with version 11 in 2018, Symbola has been copyrighted with a ban on commercial use and derivative works. Other typefaces including a significant number of emoji characters include <a href="/wiki/Noto_fonts" title="Noto fonts">Noto Emoji</a>, Adobe Source Emoji, and <a href="/wiki/Quivira_(typeface)" title="Quivira (typeface)">Quivira</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li>The 2009 film <i><a href="/wiki/Moon_(2009_film)" title="Moon (2009 film)">Moon</a></i> featured a robot named GERTY who communicates using a neutral-toned synthesized voice together with a screen showing emoji representing the corresponding emotional content.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> acquired an emoji version of <a href="/wiki/Herman_Melville" title="Herman Melville">Herman Melville</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Moby_Dick" class="mw-redirect" title="Moby Dick">Moby Dick</a></i> created by Fred Benenson.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>A musical called <i>Emojiland</i> premiered at Rockwell Table &amp; Stage in Los Angeles in May 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-playbill.com_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-playbill.com-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timeout.com_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeout.com-82">[81]</a></sup> after selected songs were presented at the same venue in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>In October 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Museum of Modern Art">Museum of Modern Art</a> acquired the original collection of emoji distributed by NTT Docomo in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>In November 2016, the first emoji-themed convention, Emojicon, was held in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>In March 2017, the first episode of <a href="/wiki/Samurai_Jack_(season_5)" title="Samurai Jack (season 5)">the fifth season of <i>Samurai Jack</i></a> featured alien characters who communicate in emoji.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>In April 2017, the <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Smile_(Doctor_Who)" title="Smile (Doctor Who)">Smile</a>" featured nanobots called Vardy, which communicate through robotic avatars that use emoji (without any accompanying speech output) and are sometimes referred to by the time travelers as "Emojibots".<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>On July 28, 2017, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Animation" title="Sony Pictures Animation">Sony Pictures Animation</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emoji_Movie" title="The Emoji Movie">The Emoji Movie</a></i>, a 3D computer animated movie featuring the voices of <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">Patrick Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sof%C3%ADa_Vergara" title="Sofía Vergara">Sofía Vergara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Faris" title="Anna Faris">Anna Faris</a>, <a href="/wiki/T._J._Miller" class="mw-redirect" title="T. J. Miller">T. J. Miller</a>, and other notable actors and comedians.<sup id="cite_ref-Dec2015CS_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dec2015CS-182">[181]</a></sup></li>
      </ul>

             <tr>
              <th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Symbols in braille</th>
              <td class="navbox-list navbox-even hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
               <div style="padding:0em 0.25em"> 
                <ul>
                 <li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Braille_music" title="Braille music">Braille music</a></span></li> 
                 <li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Canadian_currency_tactile_feature" title="Canadian currency tactile feature">Canadian currency marks</a></span></li> 
                 <li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Computer_Braille_Code" title="Computer Braille Code">Computer Braille Code</a></span></li> 
                 <li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Gardner%E2%80%93Salinas_braille_codes" title="Gardner–Salinas braille codes">Gardner–Salinas braille codes</a> (science; GS8/GS6)</span></li> 
                 <li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/IPA_Braille" title="IPA Braille">International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)</a></span></li>
